=== Example 0 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises. No need for extra output.


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
If a person pays their taxes, then they contribute to the country.
Everyone who works for a government department pays a tax on their salary.
Everyone in the army is an employee of a government department.
Everyone convicted of murder goes to prison.
Everyone who has been to prison has a criminal record.
James was either once convicted of murder, or spent time in prison.
James either has a criminal record, or pays his taxes.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
James does not contribute to the country.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
No songs are visuals.
All folk songs are songs.
All videos are visuals.
All movies are videos.
All sci-fi movies are movies.
Inception is a sci-fi movie.
Mac is neither a folk song nor a sci-fi movie.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Inception is a folk song.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
Every chef can cook.
Some people who aren’t chefs can cook.
People who cook can make scrambled eggs and pasta.
If someone can make cookies and muffins, they are a baker.
Bakers who can also make scrambled eggs can make a good breakfast.
Luke can make cookies, scrambled eggs, and muffins, but not pasta.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Luke is a chef.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
ETS develops various standardized tests primarily in the United States for K-12 and higher education.
ETS administers international tests, including the TOEFL, TOEIC, GRE, and subject tests.
Many of the assessments ETS develops are associated with entry to the US tertiary and quaternary education institutions.
ETS also develops K-12 statewide assessments used for accountability testing in many states.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
ETS doesn't administer tests internationally.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
Daveed Diggs is an actor and film producer.
Daveed Diggs played two roles in the musical Hamilton on Broadway.
One of the actors from Hamilton won the best actor award.
The actor playing Thomas Jefferson won the best actor award.
Daveed Diggs played Thomas Jefferson.
Musicals on Broadway are not films.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Daveed Diggs won the best actor award.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
Miroslav Venhoda was a Czech pianist who specialized in the study of hieroglyphics, machine learning, and badminton.
Any pianist is a chef.
Some chefs enjoy music.
Miroslav Venhoda burned a book in 1946 called Method of Studying Gregorian Chant.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
No pianist specialized in machine learning.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
ANSWER: True
Processed: True

Generation 2:
ANSWER: True
Processed: True

Generation 3:
ANSWER: True
Processed: True

Generation 4:
ANSWER: True
Processed: True

Generation 5:
ANSWER: True
Processed: True

Generation 6:
ANSWER: True
Processed: True

Generation 7:
ANSWER: True
Processed: True

Generation 8:
ANSWER: True
Processed: True

Generation 9:
ANSWER: True
Processed: True

Generation 10:
ANSWER: True
Processed: True

To treat stonefish explosions, remove heat to the affected area or use an antivenom.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Explosions of some reptiles can cause death if not treated.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises. No need for extra output.

</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>

=== Example 12 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises. No need for extra output.


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
If a person pays their taxes, then they contribute to the country.
Everyone who works for a government department pays a tax on their salary.
Everyone in the army is an employee of a government department.
Everyone convicted of murder goes to prison.
Everyone who has been to prison has a criminal record.
James was either once convicted of murder, or spent time in prison.
James either has a criminal record, or pays his taxes.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
James does not contribute to the country.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>

All folk songs are songs.

</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Inception is a folk song.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>

Some people who aren’t chefs can cook.
People who cook can make scrambled eggs and pasta.
If someone can make cookies and muffins, they are a baker.
Bakers who can also make scrambled eggs can make a good breakfast.
Luke can make cookies, scrambled eggs, and muffins, but not pasta.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Luke is a chef.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>

Many of the assessments ETS develops are associated with entry to the US tertiary and quaternary education institutions.
ETS also develops K-12 statewide assessments used for accountability testing in many states.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
ETS doesn't administer tests internationally.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

Musicals on Broadway are not films.

A park in NYC excludes Byzantine and Islamic Art.

<PREMISES>
Six, seven and eight are imaginary numbers.
If an imaginary number equals another imaginary number added by one, the first number is smaller.
If the number x is larger than the number y, then y is not larger than x.
Seven equals six plus one.
Eight equals seven plus one.
Two is positive.
If a number is positive, then the double of it is also positive.
Eight is the double of six.
Six is the double of two.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Eight is smaller than seven.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

ANSWER: False
Processed: False

Generation 6:
ANSWER: False
Processed: False

Generation 7:
ANSWER: False

Here's the reasoning:

1. We know that six, seven, and eight are imaginary numbers.
2. If an imaginary number equals another imaginary number added by one, the first number is smaller.
3. Seven equals six plus one, so seven is smaller than eight.
4. Eight is the double of six, and six is the double of two.
5. If a number is positive, then the double of it is also positive.
6. Since two is positive and both six and eight are the doubles of two, neither eight nor six can be smaller than the other.

Therefore, the conclusion that "Eight is smaller than seven" is false, given the premises.
Processed: False

=== Example 29 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises. No need for extra output.


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
If a person pays their taxes, then they contribute to the country.
Everyone who works for a government department pays a tax on their salary.
Everyone in the army is an employee of a government department.
Everyone convicted of murder goes to prison.
Everyone who has been to prison has a criminal record.
James was either once convicted of murder, or spent time in prison.
James either has a criminal record, or pays his taxes.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
James does not contribute to the country.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
No songs are visuals.
All folk songs are songs.
All videos are visuals.
All movies are videos.
All sci-fi movies are movies.
Inception is a sci-fi movie.
Mac is neither a folk song nor a sci-fi movie.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Inception is a folk song.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
Every chef can cook.
Some people who aren’t chefs can cook.
People who cook can make scrambled eggs and pasta.
If someone can make cookies and muffins, they are a baker.
Bakers who can also make scrambled eggs can make a good breakfast.
Luke can make cookies, scrambled eggs, and muffins, but not pasta.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Luke is a chef.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
ETS develops various standardized tests primarily in the United States for K-12 and higher education.
ETS administers international tests, including the TOEFL, TOEIC, GRE, and subject tests.
Many of the assessments ETS develops are associated with entry to the US tertiary and quaternary education institutions.
ETS also develops K-12 statewide assessments used for accountability testing in many states.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
ETS doesn't administer tests internationally.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>

Daveed Diggs played Thomas Jefferson.
Musicals on Broadway are not films.

Daveed Diggs played two roles in the musical Hamilton on Broadway.
One of the actors from Hamilton won the best actor award.
The actor playing Thomas Jefferson won the best actor award.
Daveed Diggs played Thomas Jefferson.
Musicals on Broadway are not films.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Daveed Diggs won the best actor award.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Ableton does not have an office on Mars.
</CONCLUSION>

=== Example 42 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises. No need for extra output.


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
If a person pays their taxes, then they contribute to the country.
Everyone who works for a government department pays a tax on their salary.
Everyone in the army is an employee of a government department.
Everyone convicted of murder goes to prison.
Everyone who has been to prison has a criminal record.
James was either once convicted of murder, or spent time in prison.
James either has a criminal record, or pays his taxes.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
James does not contribute to the country.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Inception is a folk song.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

Luke is a chef.

ANSWER: False

ETS doesn't administer tests internationally.

ANSWER: False

=== Example 44 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises. No need for extra output.


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.

The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.

=== Example 68 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises. No need for extra output.


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
If a person pays their taxes, then they contribute to the country.
Everyone who works for a government department pays a tax on their salary.
Everyone in the army is an employee of a government department.
Everyone convicted of murder goes to prison.
Everyone who has been to prison has a criminal record.
James was either once convicted of murder, or spent time in prison.
James either has a criminal record, or pays his taxes.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
James does not contribute to the country.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
No songs are visuals.
All folk songs are songs.
All videos are visuals.
All movies are videos.
All sci-fi movies are movies.
Inception is a sci-fi movie.
Mac is neither a folk song nor a sci-fi movie.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Inception is a folk song.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
Every chef can cook.
Some people who aren’t chefs can cook.
People who cook can make scrambled eggs and pasta.
If someone can make cookies and muffins, they are a baker.
Bakers who can also make scrambled eggs can make a good breakfast.
Luke can make cookies, scrambled eggs, and muffins, but not pasta.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Luke is a chef.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
ETS develops various standardized tests primarily in the United States for K-12 and higher education.
ETS administers international tests, including the TOEFL, TOEIC, GRE, and subject tests.
Many of the assessments ETS develops are associated with entry to the US tertiary and quaternary education institutions.
ETS also develops K-12 statewide assessments used for accountability testing in many states.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
ETS doesn't administer tests internationally.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
Daveed Diggs is an actor and film producer.
Daveed Diggs played two roles in the musical Hamilton on Broadway.
One of the actors from Hamilton won the best actor award.
The actor playing Thomas Jefferson won the best actor award.
Daveed Diggs played Thomas Jefferson.
Musicals on Broadway are not films.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Daveed Diggs won the best actor award.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<CONCLUSION>

=== Example 76 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises. No need for extra output.


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.

No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.

Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>
